human services for the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027; and
to provide for the expenditure of the appropriations.

20 Services.

25 services.

16 Sec. 204. A department or agency shall use the internet to
17 fulfill the reporting requirements of this part, make each report
18 readily accessible to the public, and conspicuously post each
19 required report in a single archivable location on the department's
20 or agency's Michigan.gov website not later than the due date
21 required for each report. In addition to placing all reports
22 required in the current fiscal year on the department's or agency's
23 website, the department or agency shall maintain on its website all
24 reports placed on the website from previous fiscal years posted by
25 fiscal year in the same single archivable location. The department
26 or agency shall also transmit all required reports for the current
27 fiscal year to the standard report recipients and any other
28 required recipients by email.

1 management and budget act, 1984 PA 431, MCL 18.1261, all of the

3 (a) The funds must not be used for the purchase of foreign
4 goods or services, or both, if competitively priced and of

EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n

1 (a) Affect the operations of the department, including
2 reductions in federal revenue. For federal revenue reductions, the

5 the following information:
6 (i) The amount of additional state revenue required to replace

13 department or agency.

4 the law of this state to collect an overpayment owed to the
5 department, beginning 60 days after the initial notification date

9 date of the overpayment amount. The department shall not collect
10 penalty interest in an amount that exceeds the amount of the
11 original overpayment. This state's share of any funds collected
12 under this section must be deposited in the general fund of this
13 state.

3 CHILD SUPPORT ENFORCEMENT
4 Sec. 401. (1) The appropriations in part 1 assume a total
5 federal child support incentive payment of $26,500,000.00.
6 (2) From the federal money received for child support
7 incentive payments, $12,000,000.00 must be retained by this state
8 and expended for child support program expenses.
9 (3) From the federal money received for child support
10 incentive payments, $14,500,000.00 must be paid to counties based
11 on each county's performance level for each of the performance
12 measures under 45 CFR 305.2.
13 (4) If the child support incentive payment to this state from
14 the federal government is greater than $26,500,000.00, then 100% of
15 the amount in excess must be retained by this state and is
16 appropriated until the total retained by this state reaches
17 $15,397,400.00.
18 (5) If the child support incentive payment to this state from
19 the federal government is greater than the amount needed to satisfy
20 subsections (1), (2), (3), and (4), the additional funds are
21 subject to appropriation by the legislature.
22 (6) If the child support incentive payment to this state from
23 the federal government is less than $26,500,000.00, then the state
24 share and the county share must each be reduced by 50% of the
25 shortfall.
26 Sec. 409. (1) If statewide retained child support collections
27 exceed $38,300,000.00, 75% of the amount in excess of
28 $38,300,000.00 is appropriated to legal support contracts. The
29 excess appropriation may be distributed to eligible counties to
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n
58
1 supplement, but not supplant, county title IV-D funding.
2 (2) Each county whose retained child support collections in
3 the current fiscal year exceed its fiscal year 2004-2005 retained
4 child support collections, excluding tax offset and financial
5 institution data match collections in both the current fiscal year
6 and fiscal year 2004-2005, shall receive its proportional share of
7 the 75% excess appropriation.
8 Sec. 410. (1) If title IV-D-related child support collections
9 are escheated, the state budget director is authorized to adjust

4 Sec. 601. After a client agrees to the release of the client's
5 name and address to the local housing authority, the department

7 regarding whether the housing unit for which vendoring has been

13 Sec. 602. The department shall conduct a full evaluation of an
14 individual's assistance needs if the individual has applied for
15 disability more than 1 time in a 1-year period.
16 Sec. 603. For any change in the income of a recipient of the
17 food assistance program, the family independence program, or state
18 disability assistance that results in a benefit decrease, the
19 department shall notify the recipient of the amount of the decrease
20 not later than 15 work days before the first day of the month in
21 which the decrease takes effect.
22 Sec. 604. (1) From the funds appropriated in part 1 for state
23 disability assistance payments, the department shall operate a
24 state disability assistance program. Except as provided in
25 subsection (3), to be eligible for the program, an individual must
26 be a needy citizen of the United States or alien exempted from the
27 SSI citizenship requirement who is not less than 18 years of age,
28 or an emancipated minor, and meets 1 or more of the following
29 requirements:
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n
87
1 (a) Is a recipient of SSI, Social Security, or medical
2 assistance due to disability or being 65 years of age or older.
3 (b) Is an individual with a physical or mental impairment that
4 meets federal SSI disability standards, except that the minimum
5 duration of the disability must be 90 days. Substance use disorder
6 alone is not a basis for eligibility.
7 (c) Is a resident of an adult foster care facility, a home for
8 the aged, a county infirmary, or a substance use disorder treatment
9 center.
10 (d) Is an individual receiving 30-day postresidential
11 substance use disorder treatment.
12 (e) Is an individual diagnosed as having AIDS.
13 (f) Is an individual receiving special education services
14 through a local intermediate school district.
15 (g) Is a caretaker of a disabled individual who meets the
16 requirements specified in subdivision (a), (b), (e), or (f).
17 (2) An applicant for or recipient of state disability
18 assistance is considered needy if the applicant or recipient does
19 both of the following:
20 (a) Meets the same asset test as is applied for the family
21 independence program.
22 (b) Has a monthly budgetable income that is less than the
23 payment standards.
24 (3) Except for an individual described in subsection (1)(c) or
25 (d), an individual is not disabled under this section if the
26 individual's drug addiction or alcoholism is a contributing factor
27 material to the determination of disability.
28 (4) As used in this section:
29 (a) "Material to the determination of disability" means that,
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n
88
1 if the individual stopped using drugs or alcohol, the individual's
2 remaining physical or mental limitations would not be disabling. If
3 the individual's remaining physical or mental limitations would be
4 disabling, then the drug addiction or alcoholism is not material to
5 the determination of disability and the individual may receive
6 state disability assistance, but the individual must actively
7 participate in a substance abuse treatment program, and the
8 assistance must be paid to a third party or through vendor
9 payments.
10 (b) "Substance abuse treatment" includes receipt of inpatient
11 or outpatient services or participation in Alcoholics Anonymous or
12 a similar program.

8 EPIDEMIOLOGY, EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES, AND LABORATORY
9 Sec. 1180. From the funds appropriated in part 1 for
10 epidemiology administration and for childhood lead program, the
11 department shall maintain a public health drinking water program
12 and maintain enhanced efforts to monitor child blood lead levels.
13 The public health drinking water program shall ensure that
14 appropriate investigations of potential health hazards occur for
15 all community and noncommunity drinking water supplies where
16 chemical exceedances of action levels, health advisory levels, or
17 maximum contaminant limits are identified. The goals of the
18 childhood lead program must include improving the identification of
19 children affected by lead exposure, improving the timeliness of
20 case follow-up, and attaining nurse care management for children
21 with lead exposure, and to achieve a long-term reduction in the
22 percentage of children in this state with elevated blood lead
23 levels.

9 Sec. 1965. (1) From the funds appropriated in part 1 for water

11 grants to qualified providers to assist eligible residents who have
12 a financial burden, have accumulated a balance on their water
13 utility bill, have had their water service shut off, and/or are at
14 risk of having their water service shut off. Eligible expenditures
15 from these funds must be income-based and must include all of the
16 following:
17 (a) Restoring residential water service.
18 (b) Paying down water bills currently in arrears.
19 (c) Supporting reasonable water affordability plans that are
20 based on an individual's ability to pay, including capped payments
21 based on household income to prevent accumulating a balance on
22 future water bills and funding to qualified providers to cover the
23 remaining cost of service.
24 (d) Protecting participating residents from water shutoffs.
25 (2) To be considered a qualified provider under this section,
26 the provider must be 1 of the following:
27 (a) A community water system.
28 (b) A community action agency.
29 (c) A nonprofit, community-based organization organized under
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n
190
1 the laws of this state that is exempt from federal income tax under
2 section 501(c)(3) of the internal revenue code of 1986, 26 USC 501,
3 with a history of doing utility assistance work.

5 may spend not more than 3% of the total grant award for
6 administrative services related to the implementation of this
7 section.
8 (4) Qualified providers receiving grants under this section

19 (e) The number of individual applicants denied assistance.

16 Sec. 204. A department or agency shall use the internet to
17 fulfill the reporting requirements of this part, make each report
18 readily accessible to the public, and conspicuously post each
19 required report in a single archivable location on the department's
20 or agency's Michigan.gov website not later than the due date
21 required for each report. In addition to placing all reports
22 required in the current fiscal year on the department's or agency's
23 website, the department or agency shall maintain on its website all
24 reports placed on the website from previous fiscal years posted by
25 fiscal year in the same single archivable location. The department
26 or agency shall also transmit all required reports for the current
27 fiscal year to the standard report recipients and any other
28 required recipients by email.
29 Sec. 205. To the extent permissible under section 261 of the
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n

32
1 management and budget act, 1984 PA 431, MCL 18.1261, all of the
2 following apply to the expenditure of funds appropriated in part 1:
3 (a) The funds must not be used for the purchase of foreign
4 goods or services, or both, if competitively priced and of
5 comparable quality American goods or services, or both, are
6 available.
7 (b) Preference must be given to goods or services, or both,
8 manufactured or provided by Michigan businesses, if they are
9 competitively priced and of comparable quality.
10 (c) Preference must be given to goods or services, or both,
11 that are manufactured or provided by Michigan businesses owned and
12 operated by veterans, if they are competitively priced and of
13 comparable quality.

EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n

1 (a) Affect the operations of the department, including
2 reductions in federal revenue. For federal revenue reductions, the

5 the following information:
6 (i) The amount of additional state revenue required to replace
7 the lost federal revenue.
8 (ii) The services the department or agency will have to reduce

12 regulated or served by, or that otherwise engages with, the
13 department or agency.
14 (c) Create a regulatory gap that could negatively impact the

16 (d) Increase the department's or agency's costs.

3 CHILD SUPPORT ENFORCEMENT
4 Sec. 401. (1) The appropriations in part 1 assume a total
5 federal child support incentive payment of $26,500,000.00.
6 (2) From the federal money received for child support
7 incentive payments, $12,000,000.00 must be retained by this state
8 and expended for child support program expenses.
9 (3) From the federal money received for child support
10 incentive payments, $14,500,000.00 must be paid to counties based
11 on each county's performance level for each of the performance
12 measures under 45 CFR 305.2.
13 (4) If the child support incentive payment to this state from
14 the federal government is greater than $26,500,000.00, then 100% of
15 the amount in excess must be retained by this state and is
16 appropriated until the total retained by this state reaches
17 $15,397,400.00.
18 (5) If the child support incentive payment to this state from
19 the federal government is greater than the amount needed to satisfy
20 subsections (1), (2), (3), and (4), the additional funds are
21 subject to appropriation by the legislature.
22 (6) If the child support incentive payment to this state from
23 the federal government is less than $26,500,000.00, then the state
24 share and the county share must each be reduced by 50% of the
25 shortfall.
26 Sec. 409. (1) If statewide retained child support collections

28 $38,300,000.00 is appropriated to legal support contracts. The
29 excess appropriation may be distributed to eligible counties to
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n

58
1 supplement, but not supplant, county title IV-D funding.

22 Sec. 604. (1) From the funds appropriated in part 1 for state
23 disability assistance payments, the department shall operate a
24 state disability assistance program. Except as provided in
25 subsection (3), to be eligible for the program, an individual must
26 be a needy citizen of the United States or alien exempted from the
27 SSI citizenship requirement who is not less than 18 years of age,
28 or an emancipated minor, and meets 1 or more of the following
29 requirements:
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n

87
1 (a) Is a recipient of SSI, Social Security, or medical
2 assistance due to disability or being 65 years of age or older.
3 (b) Is an individual with a physical or mental impairment that
4 meets federal SSI disability standards, except that the minimum
5 duration of the disability must be 90 days. Substance use disorder
6 alone is not a basis for eligibility.
7 (c) Is a resident of an adult foster care facility, a home for
8 the aged, a county infirmary, or a substance use disorder treatment
9 center.
10 (d) Is an individual receiving 30-day postresidential
11 substance use disorder treatment.
12 (e) Is an individual diagnosed as having AIDS.
13 (f) Is an individual receiving special education services
14 through a local intermediate school district.
15 (g) Is a caretaker of a disabled individual who meets the
16 requirements specified in subdivision (a), (b), (e), or (f).
17 (2) An applicant for or recipient of state disability
18 assistance is considered needy if the applicant or recipient does
19 both of the following:
20 (a) Meets the same asset test as is applied for the family
21 independence program.
22 (b) Has a monthly budgetable income that is less than the
23 payment standards.
24 (3) Except for an individual described in subsection (1)(c) or
25 (d), an individual is not disabled under this section if the
26 individual's drug addiction or alcoholism is a contributing factor
27 material to the determination of disability.
28 (4) As used in this section:
29 (a) "Material to the determination of disability" means that,
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n

88
1 if the individual stopped using drugs or alcohol, the individual's
2 remaining physical or mental limitations would not be disabling. If
3 the individual's remaining physical or mental limitations would be
4 disabling, then the drug addiction or alcoholism is not material to
5 the determination of disability and the individual may receive
6 state disability assistance, but the individual must actively
7 participate in a substance abuse treatment program, and the
8 assistance must be paid to a third party or through vendor
9 payments.
10 (b) "Substance abuse treatment" includes receipt of inpatient
11 or outpatient services or participation in Alcoholics Anonymous or
12 a similar program.

23 (a) "Cost avoidance" includes expenditures avoided due to

8 EPIDEMIOLOGY, EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES, AND LABORATORY
9 Sec. 1180. From the funds appropriated in part 1 for
10 epidemiology administration and for childhood lead program, the
11 department shall maintain a public health drinking water program
12 and maintain enhanced efforts to monitor child blood lead levels.
13 The public health drinking water program shall ensure that
14 appropriate investigations of potential health hazards occur for
15 all community and noncommunity drinking water supplies where
16 chemical exceedances of action levels, health advisory levels, or
17 maximum contaminant limits are identified. The goals of the
18 childhood lead program must include improving the identification of
19 children affected by lead exposure, improving the timeliness of
20 case follow-up, and attaining nurse care management for children
21 with lead exposure, and to achieve a long-term reduction in the
22 percentage of children in this state with elevated blood lead
23 levels.
24 Sec. 1181. From the funds appropriated in part 1 for
25 epidemiology administration, the department shall maintain a vapor
26 intrusion response program. The vapor intrusion response program
27 shall assess risks to public health at vapor intrusion sites and
28 respond to vapor intrusion risks if appropriate. The goals of the
29 vapor intrusion response program must include reducing the number
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n

138
1 of individuals who are exposed to toxic substances through vapor
2 intrusion and improving health outcomes for individuals who are
3 identified as having been exposed to vapor intrusion.

5 the department shall submit a report to the standard report
6 recipients on the expenditures and activities undertaken by the
7 lead abatement program during the previous fiscal year using the
8 funds previously appropriated for the healthy homes program. The
9 report must include, but is not limited to, a funding allocation

11 subcontractor, a description of program elements, the number of
12 housing units abated of lead-based paint hazards by zip code, and a
13 description of program accomplishments and progress.

13 HEALTH SERVICES
14 Sec. 1605. The protected income level for Medicaid coverage
15 determined under section 106(1)(b)(iii) of the social welfare act,
16 1939 PA 280, MCL 400.106, is 100% of the related public assistance
17 standard.
18 Sec. 1606. For the purpose of guardian and conservator
19 charges, the department may deduct up to $83.00 per month as an
20 allowable expense against a recipient's income when determining
21 Medicaid eligibility and patient pay amounts.
22 Sec. 1607. (1) The department shall immediately presume that
23 an applicant for Medicaid whose qualifying condition is pregnancy
24 is eligible for Medicaid coverage, unless the preponderance of
25 evidence in the applicant's application indicates otherwise. The
26 applicant who is qualified as described in this subsection is
27 allowed to select or remain with the Medicaid participating
28 obstetrician of the applicant's choice.
29 (2) Each qualifying applicant is entitled to receive all
EMR S06108'26 (S-1) zthm8n

153
1 medically necessary obstetrical and prenatal care without
2 preauthorization from a health plan. All claims submitted for
3 payment for obstetrical and prenatal care must be paid at the
4 Medicaid fee-for-service rate if a contract does not exist between
5 the Medicaid participating obstetrical or prenatal care provider
6 and the managed care plan. The applicant must receive a listing of
7 Medicaid physicians and managed care plans in the immediate
8 vicinity of the applicant's residence.
9 (3) If an applicant, presumed to be eligible for Medicaid
10 under subsection (1), is subsequently found to be ineligible, a
11 Medicaid physician or managed care plan that has been providing
12 pregnancy services to the applicant is entitled to reimbursement
13 for the services until the Medicaid physician or managed care plan
14 is notified by the department that the applicant was found to be
15 ineligible for Medicaid.
16 (4) If the preponderance of evidence in an application under
17 subsection (1) indicates that the applicant is not eligible for
18 Medicaid, the department shall refer the applicant to the nearest
19 public health clinic or similar entity as a potential source for
20 receiving pregnancy-related services.
21 (5) The department shall develop an enrollment process for
22 applicants covered under this section that facilitates the
